Villare Anglicum: OR A VIEVV of the TOVVNES OF ENGLAND. Collected by the appointment of Sir HENRY SPELMAN Knight. LONDON, Printed by R. Hodgkinsonne, dwelling in Thames-street neere Baynards-Castle, 1656.
To the Reader. TRAVELLING long Journeys is costly, at all times trouble∣some, at some times dange∣rous: Yet is it both a gene∣ral and generous desire of most men to be acquainted with their native Country. To satisfie them herein, this work is set forth; where thou mayest crosse Rivers without Boat or Bridge, climbe up Mountains without pains, and goe down without danger: in a word thy eye may safely travell in a few houres over all Eng∣land,
this Book presenting the Towns and Villa∣ges thereof, alphabetically methodized, with the addition of their respective Counties, Hundreds, &c. Now know this was collected by the appoint∣ment (at the charge, and for the use) of that wor∣thy Antiquarie Sir Henry Spelman, one of whom too much cannot be said in his commendation; As who confuted that aspertion which is generally cast on Antiquaries, that they are either supercili∣ous or superstitious, either proud or popishly affected, such his humble carriage to all persons and since∣cerity in the Protestant Religion. Now it is enough to perswade others of the usefullnesse of this Treatise, that so learned a man would cause it to be composed for his private perusall; and because things of this nature the more publique the more profitable, what formerly was confined to his Study is now enlarged for the benefit of all who please to make use there∣of. None can be so unreasonable as to expect that
this Work should descend to the specifying of the names of single Houses, it being impossible∣to grinde it so small as to powder. What Dragg-Net is so capable, or can be so cast, to catch all Minams that come under it? the performance therein will be satisfactory to rational Rea∣ders if all considerable Villages be particula∣rized. Yet we believe the charitable Reader carries such a Chancery in his bosome as to pardon some omissions, if casually some places have escaped observation. Catalogues in this kinde cannot be begun and finished at once, or by one Man, (though never so industrious) but require a con∣tribution of many well disposed persons for the completing thereof. And therefore if any shall be pleased to return to the Printer hereof the names of such places as have slipt his notice, he shall have the hearty thanks for, and the World the benefit by his in∣structions in the next Edition hereof. It is also desired, that where faults are com∣mitted
in false spelling of names, such as dwell in the places (presumed the exactest Criticks in their own Orthographie) would be pleased to amend them and return their emendations, that where the tongue of this Edition hath lisped or faultered, it may speak plainer and truer in the next, if it shall survive thereunto. November 9. 1655. Thine R. H.
